<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bibliography">Bibliography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Louis_Stevenson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Bibliography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Novels">Novels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Louis_Stevenson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Novels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kidnapped_p58_(WBHole).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kidnapped_p58_%28WBHole%29.jpg/170px-Kidnapped_p58_%28WBHole%29.jpg" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kidnapped_p58_%28WBHole%29.jpg/255px-Kidnapped_p58_%28WBHole%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kidnapped_p58_%28WBHole%29.jpg/340px-Kidnapped_p58_%28WBHole%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1968" data-file-height="2804" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kidnapped_p58_(WBHole).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration from <i><a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_(novel)" title="Kidnapped (novel)">Kidnapped</a></i>. Caption: "Hoseason turned upon him with a flash" (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Kidnapped/Chapter_7" class="extiw" title="s:Kidnapped/Chapter 7">chapter VII</a>, " I Go to Sea in the Brig "Covenant" of Dysart ")</div></div></div>
<ul><li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Hair_Trunk_or_The_Ideal_Commonwealth&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Hair Trunk or The Ideal Commonwealth (page does not exist)">The Hair Trunk or The Ideal Commonwealth</a></i> (1877) Unfinished and unpublished.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> An annotated edition of the original manuscript, edited and introduced by Roger G. Swearingen, was published as <i>The Hair Trunk or The Ideal Commonwealth: An Extravaganza</i> in August 2014.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Treasure_Island" title="Treasure Island">Treasure Island</a></i> (1883) His first major success, a tale of <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a>, buried treasure, and <a href="/wiki/Adventure_novel" class="mw-redirect" title="Adventure novel">adventure</a>, has been filmed frequently. In an 1881 letter to W. E. Henley, he provided the earliest known title, "The Sea Cook, or Treasure Island: a Story for Boys".</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Prince_Otto" title="Prince Otto">Prince Otto</a></i> (1885) Stevenson's third full-length narrative, an action romance set in the imaginary Germanic state of Grünewald.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Strange_Case_of_Dr_Jekyll_and_Mr_Hyde" title="Strange Case of Dr Jekyll and Mr Hyde">Strange Case of Dr Jekyll and Mr Hyde</a></i> (1886), a novella about a <a href="/wiki/Dissociative_identity_disorder" title="Dissociative identity disorder">dual personality</a> much depicted in plays and films, also influential in the growth of understanding of the subconscious mind through its treatment of a kind and intelligent physician who turns into a <a href="/wiki/Psychopath" class="mw-redirect" title="Psychopath">psychopathic</a> monster after imbibing a drug intended to separate good from evil in a personality.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Kidnapped_(novel)" title="Kidnapped (novel)">Kidnapped</a></i> (1886) is a historical novel that tells of the boy David Balfour's pursuit of his inheritance and his alliance with <a href="/wiki/Alan_Breck_Stewart" title="Alan Breck Stewart">Alan Breck Stewart</a> in the intrigues of <a href="/wiki/Jacobitism" title="Jacobitism">Jacobite</a> troubles in Scotland.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Black_Arrow:_A_Tale_of_the_Two_Roses" title="The Black Arrow: A Tale of the Two Roses">The Black Arrow: A Tale of the Two Roses</a></i> (1888) An historical <a href="/wiki/Adventure_novel" class="mw-redirect" title="Adventure novel">adventure novel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romance_novel" title="Romance novel">romance</a> set during the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Master_of_Ballantrae" title="The Master of Ballantrae">The Master of Ballantrae</a>: A Winter's Tale</i> (1889), a masterful tale of revenge, set in Scotland, America, and India.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Wrong_Box_(novel)" title="The Wrong Box (novel)">The Wrong Box</a></i> (1889); co-written with <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Osbourne" title="Lloyd Osbourne">Lloyd Osbourne</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Comic_novel" title="Comic novel">comic novel</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Tontine" title="Tontine">tontine</a>, also filmed (1966).</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Wrecker_(Stevenson_novel)" title="The Wrecker (Stevenson novel)">The Wrecker</a></i> (1892); co-written with <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Osbourne" title="Lloyd Osbourne">Lloyd Osbourne</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Catriona_(novel)" title="Catriona (novel)">Catriona</a></i> (1893), also known as <i>David Balfour,</i> is a sequel to <i>Kidnapped</i>, telling of Balfour's further adventures.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Ebb-Tide" title="The Ebb-Tide">The Ebb-Tide</a></i> (1894); co-written with <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Osbourne" title="Lloyd Osbourne">Lloyd Osbourne</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Weir_of_Hermiston" title="Weir of Hermiston">Weir of Hermiston</a></i> (1896). Unfinished at the time of Stevenson's death, considered to have promised great artistic growth.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/St._Ives_(novel)" title="St. Ives (novel)">St Ives: Being the Adventures of a French Prisoner in England</a></i> (1897). Unfinished at the time of Stevenson's death, the novel was completed by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Quiller-Couch" title="Arthur Quiller-Couch">Arthur Quiller-Couch</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Short_story_collections">Short story collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Louis_Stevenson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Short story collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/New_Arabian_Nights" title="New Arabian Nights">New Arabian Nights</a></i> (1882)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/More_New_Arabian_Nights:_The_Dynamiter" title="More New Arabian Nights: The Dynamiter">More New Arabian Nights: The Dynamiter</a></i> (1885); co-written with <a href="/wiki/Fanny_Vandegrift" class="mw-redirect" title="Fanny Vandegrift">Fanny Van De Grift Stevenson</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Merry_Men_and_Other_Tales_and_Fables" title="The Merry Men and Other Tales and Fables">The Merry Men and Other Tales and Fables</a></i> (1887); contains 6 stories.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Island_Nights%27_Entertainments" title="Island Nights&#39; Entertainments">Island Nights' Entertainments</a></i> (also known as <i>South Sea Tales</i>) (1893) contains three longer stories.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Fables" class="mw-redirect" title="Fables">Fables</a></i> (1896) contains 20 stories: The persons of the tale, The sinking ship, The two matches, The sick man and the fireman, The devil and the innkeeper, The penitent, The yellow paint, The house of Eld, The four reformers, The man and his friend, The reader, The citizen and the traveller, The distinguished stranger, The carthorse and the saddlehorse, The tadpole and the frog, something in it, Faith, half faith and no faith at all, The touchstone, The poor thing, The song of the morrow.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Tales_and_Fantasies" title="Tales and Fantasies">Tales and Fantasies</a></i>, 1905, contains<i> The Story of a Lie</i>, <i>The Body Snatcher</i>, <i>The Misadventures of John Nicholson</i>.</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_works">Other works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Louis_Stevenson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><img alt="Wikisource" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/12px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" width="12" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/18px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/24px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="430" />&#160;<cite class="citation encyclopaedia">"<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/1911_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica/B%C3%A9ranger,_Pierre_Jean_de" class="extiw" title="wikisource:1911 Encyclopædia Britannica/Béranger, Pierre Jean de">Béranger, Pierre Jean de</a>". <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Eleventh_Edition" title="Encyclopædia Britannica Eleventh Edition">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i> (11th ed.). 1911.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=B%C3%A9ranger%2C+Pierre+Jean+de&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica&amp;rft.edition=11th&amp;rft.date=1911&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARobert+Louis+Stevenson" class="Z3988"></span><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r861714446">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output code.cs1-code{color:inherit;background:inherit;border:inherit;padding:inherit}.mw-parser-output .cs1-lock-free a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/9px-Lock-green.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output .cs1-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .cs1-lock-registration a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Lock-gray-alt-2.svg/9px-Lock-gray-alt-2.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output .cs1-lock-subscription a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Lock-red-alt-2.svg/9px-Lock-red-alt-2.svg.png")no-repeat;background-position:right .1em center}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration{color:#555}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription span,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration span{border-bottom:1px dotted;cursor:help}.mw-parser-output .cs1-hidden-error{display:none;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-visible-error{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration,.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-left,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}</style> — first published in the <a href="/wiki/EB9" class="mw-redirect" title="EB9">9th edition</a> (1875–1889).</li>
<li><i>Virginibus Puerisque, and Other Papers</i> (1881), contains the essays <i>Virginibus Puerisque i</i> (1876); <i>Virginibus Puerisque ii</i> (1881); <i>Virginibus Puerisque iii: On Falling in Love</i> (1877); <i>Virginibus Puerisque iv: The Truth of Intercourse</i> (1879); <i>Crabbed Age and Youth</i> (1878); <i>An Apology for Idlers</i> (1877); <i>Ordered South</i> (1874); <i>Aes Triplex</i> (1878); <i>El Dorado</i> (1878); <i>The English Admirals</i> (1878); <i>Some Portraits by Raeburn</i> (previously unpublished); <i>Child's Play</i> (1878); <i>Walking Tours</i> (1876); <i>Pan's Pipes</i> (1878); <i>A Plea for Gas Lamps</i> (1878).</li>
<li><i>Familiar Studies of Men and Books</i> (1882) containing <i>Preface, by Way of Criticism</i> (not previously published); <i>Victor Hugo's Romances</i> (1874); <i>Some Aspects of Robert Burns</i> (1879); <i>The Gospel According to Walt Whitman</i> (1878); <i>Henry David Thoreau: His Character and Opinions</i> (1880); <i>Yoshida-Torajiro</i> (1880); <i>François Villon, Student, Poet, Housebreaker</i> (1877); <i>Charles of Orleans</i> (1876); <i>Samuel Pepys</i> (1881); <i>John Knox and his Relations to Women</i> (1875).</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Memories_and_Portraits" title="Memories and Portraits">Memories and Portraits</a></i> (1887), a collection of essays.</li>
<li><i>On the Choice of a Profession</i> (1887)</li>
<li><i>Memoir of Fleeming Jenkin</i> (1888)</li>
<li><i>Father Damien: an Open Letter to the Rev. Dr. Hyde of Honolulu</i> (1890)</li>
<li><i>Vailima Letters</i> (1895)</li>
<li><i>The New Lighthouse on the Dhu Heartach Rock, Argyllshire</i> (1995). Based on an 1872 manuscript edited by R. G. Swearingen. California. Silverado Museum.</li>
<li><i>Sophia Scarlet</i> (2008). Based on 1892 manuscript edited by Robert Hoskins. AUT Media (AUT University).</li>
<li><i>Essays in the Art of Writing</i>, 1905</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poetry">Poetry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Louis_Stevenson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Poetry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/A_Child%27s_Garden_of_Verses" title="A Child&#39;s Garden of Verses">A Child's Garden of Verses</a></i> (1885), written for children but also popular with their parents. Includes such favourites as "My Shadow" and "The Lamplighter". Often thought to represent a positive reflection of the author's sickly childhood.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Underwoods" title="Underwoods">Underwoods</a></i> (1887), a collection of poetry written in both English and <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>.</li>
<li><i>Ballads</i> (1891), included <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ticonderoga:_A_Legend_of_the_West_Highlands&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ticonderoga: A Legend of the West Highlands (page does not exist)">Ticonderoga: A Legend of the West Highlands</a></i> (1887). Based on a famous Scottish ghost story.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Songs_of_Travel_and_Other_Verses" title="Songs of Travel and Other Verses">Songs of Travel and Other Verses</a></i> (1896)</li>
<li><i>Poems Hitherto Unpublished</i>, 3 vol. 1916, 1916, 1921, Boston Bibliophile Society, republished in <i>New Poems</i></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Travel_writing">Travel writing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Louis_Stevenson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Travel writing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/An_Inland_Voyage" title="An Inland Voyage">An Inland Voyage</a></i> (1878), travels with a friend in a <a href="/wiki/Rob_Roy_canoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Rob Roy canoe"><i>Rob Roy</i> canoe</a> from <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> (Belgium) to <a href="/wiki/Pontoise" title="Pontoise">Pontoise</a>, just north of Paris.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh:_Picturesque_Notes" title="Edinburgh: Picturesque Notes">Edinburgh: Picturesque Notes</a></i> (1878) - a <a href="/wiki/Paean" title="Paean">paean</a> to his birthplace, it provides Stevenson's personal introduction to each part of the city and some history behind the various sections of the city and its most famous buildings.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Travels_with_a_Donkey_in_the_C%C3%A9vennes" title="Travels with a Donkey in the Cévennes">Travels with a Donkey in the Cévennes</a></i> (1879), two weeks' solo ramble (with Modestine as his <a href="/wiki/Pack_animal" title="Pack animal">beast of burden</a>) in the mountains of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9vennes" title="Cévennes">Cévennes</a> (south-central France), one of the first books to present hiking and <a href="/wiki/Camping" title="Camping">camping</a> as <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreational activities</a>. It tells of commissioning one of the first <a href="/wiki/Sleeping_bag" title="Sleeping bag">sleeping bags</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Silverado_Squatters" title="The Silverado Squatters">The Silverado Squatters</a></i> (1883). An unconventional honeymoon trip to an abandoned mining camp in <a href="/wiki/Napa_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Napa Valley">Napa Valley</a> with his new wife Fanny and her son Lloyd. He presciently identifies the <a href="/wiki/California_wine" title="California wine">California wine</a> industry as one to be reckoned with.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Across_the_Plains_(book)" title="Across the Plains (book)">Across the Plains</a></i> (written in 1879–80, published in 1892). Second leg of his journey, by train from New York to California (then picks up with <i>The Silverado Squatters</i>). Also includes other travel essays.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Amateur_Emigrant" title="The Amateur Emigrant">The Amateur Emigrant</a></i> (written 1879–80, published 1895). An account of the first leg of his journey to California, by ship from Europe to New York. Andrew Noble (<i>From the Clyde to California: Robert Louis Stevenson's Emigrant Journey</i>, 1985) considers it to be his finest work.</li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Old_and_New_Pacific_Capitals&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Old and New Pacific Capitals (page does not exist)">The Old and New Pacific Capitals</a></i> (1882). An account of his stay in Monterey, California in August to December 1879. Never published separately. See, for example, James D. Hart, ed., <i>From Scotland to Silverado</i>, 1966.</li>
<li><i>Essays of Travel</i> (London: Chatto &amp; Windus, 1905)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Island_literature">Island literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Louis_Stevenson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Island literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although not well known, his island fiction and non-fiction is among the most valuable and collected of the 19th century body of work that addresses the Pacific area.
</p>
<ul><li><i>In the South Seas</i> (1896). A collection of Stevenson's articles and essays on his travels in the Pacific.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/A_Footnote_to_History:_Eight_Years_of_Trouble_in_Samoa" title="A Footnote to History: Eight Years of Trouble in Samoa">A Footnote to History, Eight Years of Trouble in Samoa</a></i> (1892).</li></ul>

[...] Worse still, he affected a Bohemian style, haunted the seedier parts of the Old Town, read Charles Darwin and Herbert Spencer, and declared himself an atheist.
